# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Fault Localization: iwlwifi Missing PCI Subdevice Entries

- **Repository**: torvalds/linux
- **Kernel Version**: 5.6-rc2
- **Difficulty**: expert
- **Category**: fault_localization
- **Subsystem**: Drivers
- **Component**: network-wireless (Intel iwlwifi)

## Bug Report

**Bug ID**: 206661
**Summary**: iwlwifi:9260: missing PCI subdevice entries for 0x2526 (0x04010, 0x4018 and 0x401C)
**Regression**: Yes

I am using Kernel 5.6 RC2 and I am seeing issues where firmware is not being loaded for my Intel Corporation Wireless-AC 9260 card. Attached is the boot logging.

If I can do anything to debug, let me know.

## Task

You are a fault localization agent. Given the bug report above, your task is to identify the **exact source file(s)** and **function(s)/data structure(s)** in the Linux kernel source tree (at `/workspace`) that need to be modified to fix this bug.

You must:
1. Analyze the bug report to understand the symptoms and context
2. Search the kernel source code to identify the relevant subsystem and files
3. Narrow down to the specific file(s) and function(s)/data structure(s) that contain the bug or need modification
4. Write your findings to `/workspace/fault_localization_result.json` in the following format:

```json
{
  "buggy_files": ["path/to/file.c"],
  "buggy_functions": ["function_or_struct_name"],
  "confidence": 0.8,
  "reasoning": "Brief explanation of why these locations are the fault"
}
```

**Important**: Paths should be relative to the kernel source root (e.g., `kernel/sched/core.c`, not `/workspace/kernel/sched/core.c`).

Now I have identified the fault! Let me create a comprehensive analysis document. The issue is clear:

1. In the **pci_device_id table** (`iwl_hw_card_ids`), device 0x2526 has specific subdevice entries like 0x0034, 0x0060, etc., but **missing are the OEM/ODM subdevice IDs** (0x0010, 0x0014, 0x0018, 0x001C, 0x6010, 0x6014, 0x8010, 0x8014, 0xA014, 0xE010, 0xE014, 0x0030, 0x0038, 0x003C, 0x4030)

2. These IDs **are present** in the `iwl_dev_info_table` (lines 980-995), but without explicit pci_device_id entries, they're caught by the generic `PCI_ANY_ID` fallback (line 599) which uses `iwl9000_trans_cfg` instead of the correct device-specific config.

3. This causes firmware loading to fail for systems with these OEM subdevice IDs because the incorrect configuration is used.

83-assistanttext-
Excellent! My fault localization analysis is complete. Here's a summary of my findings:

## Fault Localization Summary

### Bug Location
**File**: `drivers/net/wireless/intel/iwlwifi/pcie/drv.c`  
**Data Structure**: `iwl_hw_card_ids` (PCI device ID table)

### Root Cause
The PCI device ID table for Intel Wireless-AC 9260 (device 0x2526) is **missing explicit entries for OEM/ODM subdevice IDs**:
- Missing: 0x0010, 0x0014, 0x0018, 0x001C (iwl9260 variants)
- Missing: 0x6010, 0x6014, 0x8010, 0x8014, 0xA014, 0xE010, 0xE014
- Missing: 0x0030, 0x0038, 0x003C, 0x4030 (iwl9560 variants)

### Why This Causes the Bug
1. These OEM subdevice IDs fall back to the **generic PCI_ANY_ID entry** (line 599) which uses `iwl9000_trans_cfg`
2. While the `iwl_dev_info_table` (lines 980-995) has the correct configurations for these specific IDs, without explicit pci_device_id entries:
   - Strict device matching requirements aren't satisfied
   - The fallback generic configuration is used instead of the device-specific configuration
3. This results in **firmware loading failures** for systems with these OEM subdevice IDs

### Confidence Level: 95%
The analysis is based on:
- Direct examination of the pci_device_id table structure
- Comparison with the iwl_dev_info_table entries
- Understanding of the PCI device matching and firmware loading mechanism in the kernel

### Result File
The fault localization result has been written to `/workspace/fault_localization_result.json`

    "drivers/net/wireless/intel/iwlwifi/pcie/drv.c"

  ],
  "confidence": 0.95,
  "reasoning": "The PCI device ID table 'iwl_hw_card_ids' for Intel Wireless-AC 9260 (device 0x2526) is missing explicit entries for OEM/ODM subdevice IDs (0x0010, 0x0014, 0x0018, 0x001C, 0x6010, 0x6014, 0x8010, 0x8014, 0xA014, 0xE010, 0xE014, 0x0030, 0x0038, 0x003C, 0x4030). These subdevice IDs are defined in the iwl_dev_info_table (lines 980-995) with correct device configurations (iwl9260_2ac_160_cfg for 9260 variants and iwl9560_2ac_160_cfg for 9560 variants), but without corresponding entries in the pci_device_id table, they fall back to the generic PCI_ANY_ID entry (line 599) which uses iwl9000_trans_cfg. This causes the driver to load with incorrect firmware configuration for devices with these OEM/ODM subdevice IDs, resulting in firmware loading failures. The fix requires adding explicit pci_device_id entries mapping these subdevice IDs to their correct device configurations."
}
